de hernie carnouse	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	of hernia
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramie is so weak that it comes from the testicles and is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And it never comes from the percussion on the testicles, and this moisture is often of different colors: or it is a declining yellow, or without red, or black, or white water, and such happens more often;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of this assembly, for if it is as white as we have said, then the abscess is shallow, that is, short and as the shape of an arrow; and does not open the blisters, because it is wet all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper towel, then the abscess is shallow with part of the arrow, and because of this one thinks that it is another arrow;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the leather of the joints and the white clearly, then it smells good; so, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all around it because its shape is as described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	And according to what comes after the joint, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure with fire, it is fitting that the patient should be made well according to his power and the fulfillment of his body; then let him lie on his back, on a low thing, and cover him with many sheets.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then let him sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right, and stretch the stick at one of the two ribs at the cure of the lungs;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the stick lit, and peel the skin of the lungs among them all along until the end of the knuckle, and cut it with a straight slash while peeling the skin of the lungs carefully according to his power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the plain of water at 1.5 large holes, and extract all the water, and then put your fingers in, and close the hole up; and do not touch the skin of the lungs, but only peel it yourself; cut off piece by piece carefully the skin from him, so that if you do not peel it well, the water will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the feather falls to your work, if you set it in its place when you have completed the work of medicine; then join the .ij. limbs from the knees to a seam, and heal it as you would other wounds until it is well.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the feather corrupted by another disease, if it is necessary that you hold the suspenders, in doubt of the decay of blood; then cut the joint to all the suspender, and extract the feather, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the aiguille is assembled into two parts together, knowing that there are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first, making it even, and wash the blood, and put in another wound wet with oil rosin.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put there another wool wet with wine and oil, and put on the 2 joints, and put over double sheets, and lay it down on all the thread which is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take .ii. drapelets, and employ the woollen cloth according to this appearance, and let them be sewed together by means of a seam in the girdle of the breeches, and one of the shoulders should press upon the fundament down to the back, and the other at the part of the hand; and that other two chins upon the .ii. angles, and may all be assembled into the loop of the breeches.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and never use the knife of cautery in place of a iron one, and it is that you press 1. cautery scalfice subtil, and cut the leather of the shoes, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white medicine which contains the water may come to light;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white medicine with it like a bird, and dry it out by means of that scalfice cautery;
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut it in all the ways that you can, until you have dried out everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the fat; and know that this work is more safe; and keep from corruption of blood, and make sure that the works of cutting are done well;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything makes you contrary, or an abscess of blood or other thing, if the cure is opposite to it, according to what is before said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and will not wait for this operation because of its horror, so make a puncture, as I have said, and it is that when you are sure by the signs which we have said that the water-remedy is alive,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Then sit the patient on a high bench; then pierce the abscess at the base all along the broad part of the jaw, and place the puncture at the long hole in the chest; and make the perforation wide so that all the water can run.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the hole, and tie it, and let the rest of the water run out, then heal the wound until the sore is well.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the stain does not let the water go out of the wound's mouth, it is necessary that you put a feather or an instrument with which one treats the water from the hydropses there; for its form is as follows: and open .i. little the wound, and know that the water returns, and is gathered after 1 month or more, and when it is gathered so as before, and thus the sick person will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this chapter on pain there are many considerations, for it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the appearances of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from the heart, and most commonly from the joints; and this is due to chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to be understood: by means of bitter and sharp moisture, which is expanded in the joints, or by impact.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the heart; and it does not cause pain, but is a grievous abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes it is a grievous and painful abscess, of fierce color, and never comes from the artery or the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is an artery, if it is contracted by the arrangement of an abscess, when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	The wound made by the piercing of a needle is contracted by its arrangement with the touching of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and it can do well to make the incision on this appearance and on the other characters;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and so you chop the cur of the cow, then hang the liver high, and the truffle white as medicine, and free the suspender from all parts of the liver.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	Now that the liver is already sodden with these new ingredients, it is therefore necessary that you take the liver and the cur.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is fresh, or in that which is within the bags, it is necessary that you deliver all of it, and chop it well.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cur is behind, it is necessary that you chop it all, and extract the liver, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are done, wrap the wound in wet wool, oil and wine, and then cure it with other remedies until it is well.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess surrounded by a wrapper-like appearance, with the softening of the testicles,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans with pain when he moves;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure for this disease is well prepared with fear as before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and we will tell you how to work on it, according to what the old one did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you sit the sick person on .i. a soft seat, and then pour the poultice liquid down their throat from both sides,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessel that are near to the penis, and wet them with the master liquid, and extend them out.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then chop with a sharp spatula from the top down over the vessels, until they are all uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then peel each part off, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then take an awl or it has .i. double thread, and tie it to the first loop where it came into view, and then quickly to the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then chop them in the middle correctly, according to the length of the body, and cut out the corrumptous moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as with others where a bow is shot, so that no vessel hits either of the balls;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For if it comes from nowhere, and all the vessels come out, then you must pull the balls from all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the wound does not lose its moisture because of the incisions of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syrup
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	"And this tear is either due to sectioning or to external application on the abdomen, and these two ways of causing pain are: by beating, jumping, braying, or lifting heavy things, and similar actions;"
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	"And the signs when it is due to external application on the ribs, are that it happens little by little over a long period of time and does not suddenly occur;"
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	"And the rib bones are even up to the very end, so that the tear does not cause the intestine to separate."
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the physician, that she brings about sudden painful trouble, and are the abscesses different appearances, separating the skin, and this for the issue of the intestine and the body away from the physician.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does it separate with the intestine, and is held in, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	In these cures of iron, for fear of it coming out.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of this work is that you command to the patient that he keep the intestine in his hand within the wound, if it can be re-entered;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then have him sit with his head between your hands, and loosen the hair.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then cut off all of the skin from the top,
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then bottle up the essence of the oil of the skin according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that it can easily come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then peel off the skin, scraping all the way down until the blisters appear;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	and place your two fingers in the opening of the crotch, between the white skin which is behind the scrotum and between the second skin.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and depart what is behind the scrotum and between the second skin; and then move to the palm of your right hand into the crotch opening, and hold the white skin on top of your left hand, and bring the scrotum up against all the skin around the groin.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to stretch out the scrotum upwards, and pull back what is above the anus.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and look with your two fingers if there is any hard or white skin wrapped around the intestine, and if you find nothing, pour it into the gut.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	And take a needle where it has .i. thick thread made of .x. threads, and the bottle in the back part dou sic, which is after the skin of the coins; after the size, then cut the heads that appear from the thread, as long as there are .iiij. threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	and then assemble one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind sic where we have said that is removed from the skin of the coins, with a strong thread of 2 parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	and then wrap the heads of the thread and bind them together with 2 parts, so that no one of the vassals who suckles them can enter the ears, so that an abscess does not come up;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and then put the thread on according to the first long thread of 2 parts, and after these 2 threads leave sic where the skin is removed from the coins, which is large for one part;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and then all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; and chop in the part which is outside the skin of the eggs, until it stops running, and the bow, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	and then introduce the moist wool in oil, and put on the wound, and put the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And no time is cauterized with the white salt that we have said, after the incision, by doubt of decay of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leaves the thread as long as it sews itself; and if it delays to sew, so let it be raised with hot water, and put on that we have said, as long as it sews itself; and then:
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and then treat the wound with another treatment until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnous
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I have never seen anyone attempt to make a cure for hernia with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancient ones said that it is made in this way, as if you tie the vassels together, after cutting on a light and lightly; and tu mettras le li sur un bois, ou il est par temps sec et sans vent.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then cut off the appendage, and cure the abscess for those who have it, as long as they are still alive; and cure it as we have said, until they are well.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	No time comes when there is a rupture in the bowels, as we have said, and open them; and do not remove any of the bowels to the outside, and if any are removed, it is little, and repair every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and wherever he stays too much in this place, if the wound or syphilis believes him, as long as the intestines are removed;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and where there is a stretching of the syphilis that is in the bowels, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then it softens and dilates the intestines and opens them;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and he is healed by cautery, as we have said above; and he is never healed by iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then place the fire cautery over the edge of the wound according to the quantity of .ii. two;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then remove the skin that is separated from the flesh, and then take the hair and place it on the edge of the skin;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and then press it perfectly to the belly, and cut the .ii. inches of skin that is on the edge of the hair, and cut the two;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then remove the head from the root, and do not cover with any medicine or extend the blade in any other way, as I have told you in the treatment of the ramose intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And then he heals by healing wounds. And when you cover the fibers, if the wound and the healing are good, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The medicine must be kept in place, and does not have a visible appearance in the incision; and the cauterization is wet in this spot, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Maitre de la cauterisation par le feu, enseigne au patient à laisser pousser les poils jusqu'à ce qu'ils soient longs et égaux; et s'il les gratte à leur base, maintenez-les immobiles jusqu'à ce qu'ils poussent.
dou chastrement	Voici la traduction du texte en anglais :

de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister

des plaies	for wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will speak about the cures for hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and because of it they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are by hitting with a stone, or cutting with an sword or a dagger, or a lance or a staff or a spear, or similar things; or
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made by the blows of the heart, such as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or on the breast, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar limbs; or

Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound appears at the top, and the bone is not broken, if you are careful it is from a stone or similar thing, and the skin is all torn and the wound is great,

se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	If you can, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	if you should cause the patient to lie down on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head,
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the region of the loins the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if the head and the breast are higher than the hip region,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if it ruptures the belly in one of the two regions,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if the hip region where it is dislocated is higher than the other,
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is necessary to treat what I have said about great wounds and painful injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds but with this you are dressed,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	and then place your hands minister pitous who covers all the wound with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and gather the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of suturing.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and you must twist a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave two spaces at the head of the wound, and thread a needle with good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the leather with the needles from the side,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	who is sozzing the leather inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather the 20 together dou siphac the 23 together
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then extract it from a double thread entor the needle of 20 parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and gather the 20 together of the wound ahead,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave them for two spaces, and I put another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then lay down the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this according to what you need with the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	as long as all the wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles fall, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles fill all the space, and the very thick ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	so that they are of moderate size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and do not push the needles too far from the edge of the hair and leather;
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie avant la soudure;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the heads of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while he is sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put blankets or sheets over the heads of the needles to keep them in place,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is sealed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of sewing with needles is most useful for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it requires a needle or .ij.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you join the leather and the fabric together with a strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have perceived these things together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if I return the needle to the part where you have begun, in the manner that one threads the thread;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch of the same size as a small nail;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is for the seven days of the week;
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound this honourable man had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was stabbed with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was from his intestines, measuring about three feet in length,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and this wound is inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought him back his intestine after xxiiij hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound healed after xv days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the miracle was that he did not die, and this was a wonder.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not cure it with ointment, for I am in .ii. leu where one cannot find it or any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and rub cotton wool 19 times a day on the wound, and wash it with honey water until it was well.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	or I will tell you the three proper ways to sew:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and thread it from the outside in;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When she perceives the cure of disease by right, if the head of the phallus or coast or you have swallowed the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and pierce it from another part from within until it reaches the exterior;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and he should know about this stitch so that you also sew like the furrier sews the pelts,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the phallus on one side and the other on it until the stitch is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of suturing, which is properly done by Galens
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is if there is no thread, which joins the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the chiefs to the other chief in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	file an awl or needle near the Miramich chief, and pierce it only once,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the .ij. shoulders of the sick
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outer part to the inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as shoulders of the sick.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce the other two from the outer part to the inside, in 2 other shoulders that are opposite sides of the body;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the manner of sewing, and the most common way.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Here are the first two lines translated into English:
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	"It is necessary to sew the abdomen with .ij. needles, or each one have thread."
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	"and must one needle be pushed from one side, and the other from the other, in the way of those who sew with thread."
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the navel,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	that is the suturing more painful than those of other places in the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	the assessment of the wound is such as that of the other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and when you find the fresh wound, so that the fire has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you reset the bowel, and rub it; then put the powder on gently massaging,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the meat is moved, place any ointment that is present on it, as much as the wound;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and chop the flesh, and let the sinew be tied, and the mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would with others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to go out, cotton wisp,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it. 15 times a day until it is well.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases, when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will not connect to the main members;
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	If it is necessary for you to soak another light object in oil of time/temperature heat, or in oil of roses,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it between the arms, and clean out the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it hurts or feels warm, and often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If the wine blackens and causes burning, and sometimes comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and the perforation inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, so it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is torn,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is due to the shape of the veins and the subtlety of the whole body, and the nearness of its nature to that of children.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound jumps from the pain, so it is set back as well as the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turning towards black, that you lie the place which is black, that does not come from blood,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then hold what is between the links,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two chains hanging from the side of the wound away from it until the extraction is complete when the hair pulls, and the wound opens.
de la routure dou boueil	about the piercing of a boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one can restore it in some places,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	for I have seen some honourable men wounded or slain by a lance,
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and this wound was on the right side of the abdomen,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became infected and developed a discharge, and had wind and gas.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I could find, and did not stop until he was well, and sewed up the wound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sewn up, I doubted that the disease was in his abdomen;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there is no harm, but delay in better dispositions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and said no experiments that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in some way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take nails from great testicles, then join the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the nails have opened the mouth, so that it is placed on the iij. lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if she extorts her mouth upwards.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he holds her head, and that way it stays put so it cannot be released,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then he puts on another bandage after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and then he bandages the wound;
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If this is burning within the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and it can be tied with a fine thread cut from the intestines of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine that is completely removed,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then place at the head of this thread .i. a thin twine of flax twisted
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the string in the needle, and cut the intestine, and retie it in the suture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of sewing with thread is only good according to the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, mostly when it is in one of the internal grooves, then there is no need for surgery, but only for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	I know that any wound or abscess, once it has healed, is called a "fistula" universally.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most often when it is cut and sewn up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And the fistula is according to the green seed of the plant that grows hard and white, or one does not feel pain there.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also called the horse's tail.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never clear in a jump, and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and never pokes, and sometimes enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no cure,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	It is because of only one of these 29 causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	This is to say, namely, by the small wound or piercing.
ou por sa malice;	or due to its malignity;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has a hard core within, and on the lips, which does not allow them to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Where there is too much bowels.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the bowels are putrefied, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where because corruption is a way of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	For by its own property, in the late region there is late digestion, and late health, and it flees by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have also described all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I make known to you the cure for fistula, which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	I see that fistula can occur in all limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas which come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the syrup, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if there is part that comes to the property of the main member, and similar moves.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are great damage, and there is only work, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the light until I have said it, and you are engaged in its cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it clearly, so take a piece of leather or iron, if the fistula is straight, if you seek it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if his fistula is twisted, so that the search for a fine hook to pull,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For the plunges are bent due to the twistiness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if his fistula is deeply injured and you cannot well search for it with hooks,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	so that the cautery by fire goes into one of the injuries,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For the moisture is short from one hole to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then ask if there is bone or nerve, and chop it off completely,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient if he feels pain when you squeeze his hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know for sure where it is, whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	Here is the translation of the text:
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and bones were broken and corroded pieces of flesh that were inside them;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until she is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and the opening of the scar should be very deep from the right place, so that you cut it perfectly, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	and I put wet medicine on it, and I bottled it up to the top of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the excess that is retained at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and I put honey in it, mixed with holy oil, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healthy with this, then the fire cautery as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if his eye is corrupted by the fistula, then the patch.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	For in the vein or neck where the main members are, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if his eye is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, if the king is as long as the corruption is all bone,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with cauterization things that are dangerous to the health as long as he is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not healed, and goes back to the same way as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	knowing that you have not come all the way here
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you discover and wait until you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and bone all the corruption, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is healthy then that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too perfect, so you can't come there;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way to cure except by nature's means;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a little rotten bone, and you can pull it at the claws,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	If the extraction is made with .i. a suitable instrument for this,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is only one bone, and the tract is short, do not leave any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no doubt or fear;
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If the extraction is done with ease and without pain,
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place upon the wound something that encourages putrefaction.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh around the bone is rotten.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a large bone, like a leg or thigh.
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	If you wait so long for corruption until the blackness is all bone,
puis restoure la plaie;	Then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a great deal of corruption and it comes to little more than the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	If it is suitable and can be covered all the way up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is closed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula which happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man aged 18 to 20 years who had a pain in his leg due to an internal cause,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	For the matter came to the leg, and was escaped by a large abscess, and had no apparent cause for opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but if it is overdone by their madness on that they open on the abscess,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in corroding matter, and becoming a fistula, and it came to such a degree that all went out of the bowels and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many I have cured in iij. years, and there was no cure for me in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	for as long as I was called, and I saw a leg and the medicines with which it was cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those who run through the cracks with great noise;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and their bodies became red when they were young, and had an orange hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I put up a tent in one of these cracks, and then searched all the cracks.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came between the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I quickly went to one of the openings and began to dig until I uncovered part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it rotten and destroyed, and the rot extended all the way down to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what kind of bone it was, and I made sure that there wasn't any other rot present, except for the one that I had already uncovered;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and it didn't heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the continuous decay in the bone, and the socket, and then I took the bone, and bent over to weld the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not weld the joint with my hand on the bone, and I took it all apart;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I put it back together with medicine; and he was healed and fully welded,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and do not intend to recommend the use of this remedy except for the weakness of the disease, which cannot stand it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and from the fear of death that I have for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For with the evacuation of blood it was often, but he was completely healed, and
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and bore in place of the bone a hard core, and was of good disposition and had no harm or opposite in all, nor to air nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if his jaw is broken in any place of the chest, then it is fit to do this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take a line, and stretch it to the head of the bone which is open
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command any that he stretches upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another line of a larger size than the first line, and stretch it over the chisel which is on top of the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and set the head, so that you carry the rotten cart to the end,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the cart on top of the frame where you see the rope, so that the rope does not damage the cart;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put .I. a piece of wood or a table made of wood to support the frame so as not to damage the rotten cart;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary as much as possible to see and feel the corruption, and be also another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if his nose is corrupted, and does not open, and corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then discover the chest entirely; then put
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then tie one part of the corruption to the other with silk, and let the silk be long from the corruption; as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, so cop the joint with corrupted silk, and tie the bone or it contains from the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if corruption is in the continuation of the 19 joints, so there is another pain than that of copper;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if corruption is where he is pricked by the hand or by the foot, then it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must question that corruption, how it hurts you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not hurt you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the chisel and threads to cover these bones are many, according to the seating of the bones and the appearance of the teeth.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for each kind of work they need to be fitted with the right tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will teach you which tools you will need, according to the knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testamentary disposition of the manner of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if he takes the instrument with which you are skilled according to what it is suitable.
dou feu	do fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may be dislocated due to moisture or due to falling.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicine to remedy that corruption by the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cover that member until the place where the corruption comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes death or bad luck, which is greater, from the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the members become black, or seem to be burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then go those corrosions of member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and take it all over the body; if you hurry too much with the copper,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is through the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and witchety shark and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	then the corrosion is at the top of the head if it is struck, and do not give it space to come except with the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if the cup is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes up to the arm, if the cup is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no need for a more precise measurement of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and the corrosion comes in the first joint, if the cup comes after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if she comes where pie, so cover all pie;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if he goes up in the leg, so cover at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, so there is no other evil but to make the patient die by the fire;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of covering or sewing the member so that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister of the two strings downstream, and another ministers the other string upstream,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you remove the bag that is between the .iij. strings at .i. broad spatulum, as long as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the hood or silk, and place of each part 1. drappel linen, so that the silk does not touch the ground;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient other wound and abscess cure;
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if the pain comes when you operate, then cauterize the place well.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	Or you put on some powders that restrain it; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then wrap the member in a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there was once a man at home who had:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a darkness which seemed to be burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in his foot, so that it stained all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the honourable man saw the corruption, he washed his foot with copper, and was cured;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and a long time after, the corruption returned to him on his two hands, and came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put it upon things that reflect after the purification of the body, and cannot stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I say that I had no hope of reflecting the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the virtue of the man was weak; and he was desperate and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and wrap his copper hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no other use but to do so for the sake of others, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Now comes a time when the flesh is removed from the bone, and it takes so long that it makes a great assembly of bowels.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it ruptures and perforates, and the bone jumps out, and the viscera remain shut up, as our serfs do.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the leather that is above it is as soft as .i.. linings of sails.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	nor do they hurt the bone, nor the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends all the way to the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the burn so is that you grab the burn all around, and most when it is thin, also like us drapes;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not heat it for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have promised that the leather will be heated, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the leather is tough like a horse's hide, if you heat it with hot water:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	regardez si ses seins sont grands, et le cou qui en est est d'un odeur puante,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	So that you see if her breasts are large, and the neck which is in them is of a foul odor: then let the Egyptian medical poultice be made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take easily, and oil, and lead white, evenly, and put to cook on .i. vase at the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take this according to your need, and make it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in the cauterizing of the breast, and extract the puss.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for .ij. hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this three times, until the skin is red, and the bone is exposed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and never are they clistered with water of ash.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you squeeze ashes from a vine twig, and pour water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then pour it out, and clisterize it, until the breasts are well covered;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither can Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the paste is made of water and honey, and a little bit of chalk ground up.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you make it with honey and wine, so that the honey has the property to cleanse and wash,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine does so with a bit of strength.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done so, and you have pledged that the breasts are well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	If the cauterization causes pain in those who have it done,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and if you press an ointment of plantago, and make it with oil of roses and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cauterize it with some medicines and herbs, whose properties I have spoken of or treat with oils;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the patient has a small hole in his skin, and the cauterization cannot enter;
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if the expansion of a bit of iron, and put it in a tent of Egyptian oil,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Egyptian basilicon oil, until it is expanded;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, so that the oil or the rinse can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the cut is higher than the eye, so that the kop or lower than it is,
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is in perfect shape, so it does not slip.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you can't cover the neck properly as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the bow runs low along the string, so that it does not slip.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is in perfect shape, so it does not slip.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the loin with a cloth as you see it,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bow string comes down lightly and does not let go of the bow;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take medicines that consolidate in order to put on the back;
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and be placed on a .i. drape of linen that covers all the back;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	and place as many as possible of the opening on the left side i.e. a larger one at the front than at the back,

et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the left side in order to align the bow i.e. do not remove the large cloth before several days;

et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows what runs from the bowels, whether it is poison or pus or enough or not enough; or indigestive or indigeatable;
