et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when the medicine has spread in any way on the chest of the sick person, and you see the nature that rises from within the breast;
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is inflamed, and approach the saint;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then remove it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you remove the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if it changes .i. another cloth, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become swollen after many days, know that the breasts are not inflamed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come slowly over a long time, know that you will not perish from their poison,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the health improves. For there are men whose late healing of their wounds and those that do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and they vomit after many days, because their breasts are not yet dried up;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and their breasts are late in drying and are swollen, let them take medicines of dried substance mixed with moisture and made useful by being dried;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	for with great caution, for there is much lead in it, and that is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take care with precision, and make it with oil of rose, and anoint with even old wine.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then let it cook well, and add to it, and this same thing made better with honey cooked and thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	for when the care is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take mirr and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey as soon as it comes out of the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then in a cloth, and lay it on the chest, and never administer oil or alcohol long.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the sky, which is also like flour of times and one hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in simple or compound use: grind them, and make a powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And thus you shall know that corruption begins to spread from the bones, or hard members, or limbs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the doctor of the cure of the fistula, if as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the nail of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	is a wart that grows on the nail of the thumb of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Here is the translation of the first sentence:
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is wrapped up, and no attention is taken, then it comes .i. abscess between the toes,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and cut and grind as much as they cut at the root of the nail, and perhaps they cut all of it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corruption up to the bone, so much that it comes with stinking pain, and the two sides of the joint are large, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If it is necessary that you cut off all the excess that has been delayed from the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if he presses the foot hard, and begins to prick, and bleeds it,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	if you put the iron on the nail that pricks the foot,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pour the wine up, and hold this subtle and light foot,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on top of the remaining foot of the wine fiery and corrosive remedies to destroy all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat with garlic until he is well.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and burn it, for as long as the bone is corroded, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the pus coming out, then cut it off with a knife as described above,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is well.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and bruised, and it hurts a lot, then you must first treat it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the little finger with a chisel from one side to the other.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not go all the way down to the nail bed, because the patient will feel a lot of pain if it does.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is something, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the wrist of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	they will have a strong grip on the hands of some men by chance and are all flesh,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance they may have part bone and part flesh, and never have knuckles,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some people are born with the root of the joint, or their birth is at both ends.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those who are born without a navel do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those who are born with a navel may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the one who is chubby so is light, in some way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the size of the one who is chubby so is light, in some way: taille le en sa racine d'un large spatumile.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief à curer: si te tien dou coper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In that which is born at the root of the joint, it is painful to cure: if you should chop first the round bone up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then chop the bone with an appropriate chisel; then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The two main ways in which bones come together: either by natural birth, or by the join of a wound, or by the heat of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you believe that you have this saltpeter, so that it is repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or drapes soaked in oil, so that it does not harden;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the threads are softened, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Soaking in oil is necessary for this; take that saltpeter and, as it should be, soak it in oil so that it softens.
Des vils	Of the vile things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The evil ones are vast, wrapped in thick layers of melancholy excess, which come from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more come in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, that at others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It therefore comes that you do not administer any cleansing of the colon, and then heal from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron if it is according to .ij. manners: one is that it on the copes, and traie on fur the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another manner is that you see the vein, and trai all fur.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cut should be according to this manner: arise the first leg of the water hot very strong, until the thick blood is thin.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the leg of the sick person from above the knee to the hip;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	and cut the vein in .i. place, or in .ij. or in .iij., of a wide size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut and draw the black blood from your arm, from one hand to the other, as much as the patient can bear without fainting;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then make a poultice, and instruct him to cover himself with black meat;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the process of evacuation and cleansing when the veins are clear, and rest on the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	"For the treatment of the leg of the patient, first remove any hair: then dip it in water, and heat it; make the veins swell up red."
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	"And if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then place it against the hip at the ankle, or in the part between the knee and the ankle."
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	"Then soak the skin with oil, and peel the vein from each part, until it feels smooth when touched."
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it looks red and black, and when it enters or leather also seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pour on the resin so that it is raised from the skin, and then put on the oil lightly,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then the cope in .i. other place after it iij. do; then dry the skin on the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then let it rest at the raise, as you have done, and put on the oil to another uncinate, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	and chop another piece, or more than you need, then cut it into two pieces, and chop one of the pieces in half.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	and cut it in half, then remove it in half-inch pieces, and chop each piece in half, until it is completely removed, then chop it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then tie a strong double thread of .i.i. wire around it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and cut and lift it, and tie a string of 100 threads, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it has completely been removed.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and let it not break, for if it breaks, neither can one pull nor lift it, and there is harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished treating it, place moist wool in wine and oil over the wound and wrap it up; and heal it until it is well.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if it is twisted and bent and wrapped together, and it is not straightened, then as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if you split it diagonally, but do not cover it; and handle it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron which one takes care to curve so that it is not broken, and does not cut, but curves the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but being thick as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm areas where there are no herbs or trees, and in the ground where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance does not happen in other parts than the legs, and that which is of the pus that comes off the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	so that it comes from within the body, serpent-like and twisting, between skin and meat.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this disease are that it comes in the leg a great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the legs change, and the disease begins to grow from within, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is opened, if you wrap a piece of cloth around it from one Z and a half to I Z., and tie it up,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth hanging at the leg, and every time that there is a point to move away, if the wrap around the cloth, and the new
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too far, then cut a part of it, and wrap the rest, and do not cover its root entirely, until it is all wrapped up;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, then it enters into the hole, and causes apoplexy and corruption where it goes, and brings bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this thing, it is necessary that she be treated little by little up to the throat, and there remains nothing or a core.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and this vein never when it is treated with palm of long, or with X.,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and I have ten good hands for it, which she is of X. palm long, and when you cut her, if bottle or hole, and pierce up to the font,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and let the matter which is inside be empty, and introduce at the place healing remedies against putrefaction for a day, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And never use this hand to cut with, and least of all when it is opened in the joint of the foot or the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and then he will have a break-up, and from which he will never recover; therefore, heal it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between leather and cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	this disease is called in our land "buff disease", because it often affects buffaloes,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between leather and harness, and goes all over the body up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he smells good from one member to another, as much as he removes the leather where he goes, and jumps far.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is infected with some humor, so that they come towards him and wind and crawl and worms or eggs.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt about his malice, because when he goes through the body, and he climbs to the head, and he comes to the eyes.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	for adventure enters, and destroys the oil; and it happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drained, then one can only do so often as he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So that it is convenient that you lay it on a hard place with a very tight strap,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then drag it up and down and across, and it will be perfectly even in the cart, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery is used, until he dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it causes, if it corrupts the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the oil, then hold back its head with one hand and cut off its tail with another;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and use the patient of mondification of קורסי של תרופות פירוטיות על מנת להסיר את הרוחות הרעות,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and to wash away the meat with a poultice.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that affects certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it spreads from member to member; and I saw the one I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to attend a sick woman, and I uncovered her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and after that, he saw rise up like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	so soon as if alive silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder, and it became hard, like a bone;
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it corrupts all the body, until it comes to the other side of the breast.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she twisted again and again around her body, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how she moved her member from one part of the body to another, for I had never seen such a thing before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nonetheless, I have heard that many people have suffered great pain as their illness progressed in this way.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not want it, if I saw it in a woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this is why the woman had a small chest, and the veins were exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason does the woman's belly look tight;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and does not appear to these women who are delicious, and who have moist chests and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you have cured this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the wound heals and does not remain open, and then bandage it up tightly where it has opened;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see the hairs at their base,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure for this disease, such as pills of foul-smelling herbs, and pills of seraphim, and similar things.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	There are different types of them, there being some with large tips, and others with small ones, and some with hair-like points, and some that are welded.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some with .ij. corners, and some with tongues, and some with pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and which chies in any member so chies according to .ij. ways: or in a principle member chies,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as the brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she chies in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you hereafter, appears
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	is that you should wash yourself of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after a number of preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when there is no sign of disease yet, and the arrow has not been fully removed, lead it along and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	and the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and a medical implement is placed on top of the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a scar, and a swelling, and an irregular shape, and redness, and inflammation of the tongue, and spasms, and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and may be there is a lack of breath through the nose or ears; and may be there is a loss of speech or voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps out of the moist wound white as a pullet, and in jumping too like a burned horse;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign will reveal itself to you, if you hold it back from the cure, and follow the arrow if it is not entangled.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it points down or up is that it is near the left breast and also seems to be stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if by chance the arrow seems like a pullet, and in short black blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So then you see doubt that death may come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow is that the patient does not sweat from the wound, and the throat swells, and the skin changes color, and he gasps for breath and shivers with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters the back and causes pain and grief, and he gasps for breath, and all his limbs shake with pain.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters the stomach, perhaps it may cause an upset stomach and a foul odor to emit from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow enters the belly, and it does not go through the intestine wall, then there is no hope for healing or extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow enters the bladder, and urine flows out, causing the patient to urinate frequently, and he feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is the face and neck and throat and shoulder and ajutoire and spine and forehead and jaw and legs, and the limb resembling it, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it does not cause vomiting, as I will tell you that happened to me, then do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	A man had an arrow in his leg or armpit at the root of the nerve.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and severed the fat of the ear from the other side, and was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I saw an arrow that had entered his flesh at the root of the ear fat, severed from the paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was removed, and I only felt a poking sensation on the skin towards the ear.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and this arrow was great of an aquamarine bow, to all .i. lighter than ears; the game was healthy, and no bad accidents came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And through one arrow from the throat of a Christian, and this arrow was Arab to ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I knew the hawks, and I hid them as much as I could, and the Christians were healthy.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And through one arrow to a man, who was on his back or stomach, and I thought he died;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then let him rest for .xxx. days, if his condition does not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut off the arrow, and fixed it, and removed it, and did not suffer any bad accident to happen.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you have an arrow in your chest or back, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and do not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres natural
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, to whom he had shot an arrow into his face, and the wound was healing.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained there without suffering great pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And he shot an arrow at a prince's king, which went through his neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilted to the right side, and the arrow was completely lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been wounded. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I treated it with great care for a long time, and I did not feel any pain.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and numbness in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought this was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on Lou's plastron that atractive digestive, so that the leaks don't burst;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrows.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plastron right away, and quickly heal the wound, and delay the patient's suffering for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow. i.e. a day or two after its entry; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied to the wound an aggressive caustic medicine by hand for as long as it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tested it, and felt the tip of the arrow which took root;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied to the wound by that caustic medicine, until the tip of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and well completed the terms within three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I cut out the wound so that I took hold of the nails, and the meat from one side and the other, and I could not take it out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I ceased to be subtle and to devise ways of instruments, until I took it with very good nails,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to this person who has a certain form in the end of this chapter, as I keep it coming back and healing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I see that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I repaired it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or have you said the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your cure on what I have not said, for the book cannot include everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare a few small things, and on those that are present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	try to work with nine or ten instruments, and in the dissection of strange things which come into this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are from the limbs or they are fixed except for according to the following nine ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those who have pricked themselves there, it is an arrow entering into their flesh, and they have not pricked themselves there at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not prick now, let it be left until the flesh is rotten and the issue is healed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it has entered into the bone and cannot come out, let it be left for such a long time that it causes no harm;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it pricks, and if it does not prick, let there be a small opening at all times, so that the flesh inside is stretched, and then cut;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull, it goes just to one of the vents of the brain.
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I said happen to the patient: if you do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes just to the syph, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone of the sole, and does not come to the syph,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and let the patient stay for a few days without any further harm if the device for treating the disease is used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is badly infected and cannot be removed, if you apply tar as I told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the chest if it cannot be seen, and seek it out with all your might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, and treat it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by the stretching of the wound, and by the deepness of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone, nerve or vein, let the wound be as large as it needs to be;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and train the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can find the spot where the shaft is inserted into the bone, which is half the length of an arrow that you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or rain the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, but rather pull it out with great care.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at first, then rain it in, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of the extraction contradicts you, then apply what we have said about the cure with our章
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against incision of the nerve and vein, and do not comment on how you may pull out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or bake or roast, or firmly or loudly; and set the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow went in,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot do so, then let him do it according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where it does not open anything, or the leather is swollen in a certain place so that it can be seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly so that it enters into the bone and broadens it out, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it there still, and then begin the extraction again as long as it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is in the bone, break it off at both ends.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if he has a fever, and you see how to administer it, then he will administer .i. the instrument will be used
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the cheveur of the instrument; and then pour out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is pierced, he will pour .i. the instrument with the point entering in, for the extraction to be easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow touches the bone, so that you can cup all the marrow where the venom is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	If an arrow or spear strikes him in the chest, belly, bladder, or side, and it is close, then you may cover it with a patch.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to cover the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, for this is work.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the claw-like tools used to treat arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and it should be as follows:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of doing this: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the claw-like tool at the end should be like the beak of an owl,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	for the tip of the arrow, as it is here depicted:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of claws for gripping and for holding onto something like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the neck common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one heals are .xxxii., from which there is a head xvi.,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is the translation of the provided text into English:
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples appear.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two arms of the hair, which are called "suckers".

et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the .ij. veins which are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly referred to are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the chest, and it is called by lay people "voinne du chef";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the motion is called "fasting", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it "vein-curing"; and if the basilic is on the right side,

Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little finger is the vein between the thumb and the index finger, and if it has .i. rain;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot are .iii veins: one is located at the outer corner of the ankle joint, and

Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The ear canal, which is behind the ears, should be cleaned with old catarrh, and with headache.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the medicine, as I told you, is that you remove the head of the disease.

tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	as long as the three veins appear behind the ears, depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Here is the translation of the text line by line into English:
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lance and pierce through the vein up to the bone, and then lift your hand up towards the top of the vein.

Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood vessels that are in the two temples, if they cause headaches in old age,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and if there is pain and redness, and a habit of tears;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the blood vessel is such that I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is necessary to extract his neck until the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he must put his hand on both sides of his face, and then sign with his eyes;

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein at the forehead is as effective as the healing of the headache from ancient diseases, and it causes headaches, and bright lights.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that if the patient twists his neck, so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	and take the instrument which is called a 'spoon', whose shape is thus:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and hold firmly with your hand, or another thing, and allow the blood to flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut off the neck of the patient, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy, and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the fire must not be too hot; and the vein is cut across, because the bone is close by, and the flame might break if it is too small.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The health problems that can be helped with this are the three veins in the arms and legs that cause pain when they become inflamed or infected, and also conditions of the eye, skin rashes, and facial diseases.

Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, in case of a breeze; then make the blood run, as much as you need, and then hold it on cloth, and hold it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The patient of the birth pangs of the child so that he is well watered, and sudoriferous diseases, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as headaches and redness that come to the face, and especially when it is old;

et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long, flexible flame, and put it on the lip in the space between the iij. nostrils;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well now, and the blood will begin to run.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not over-exert yourself too much yet, and make the blood flow according to your need, then rest for a night, because it is soon restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	This is the text on the five wounds: si aide à l'estrangement de l'ailaine, et à l'encomancement de mélancolie, et à beaucoup de maladies, et à l'empétige, et à la corruption, et aux hernies, et estiomenes;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the wound is such that the patient pulls out his hair from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and if the master stands over the head of the sick person, and the sick person cuts off with .i. cut,

De la sainie des leivres	of the health of the animals
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	of the health of the mouth and teeth, and their correction, and the repair of gums, and the repairs of lips, and the growth of nails, and swelling of the tongue.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is to make the patient sit before you, and to hold his throat as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	and turn the lip, and watch as .ij. veins, one is at the right lip and the other is at the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and know them by what they are black, and because between them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then turn one and the other, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt about it,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then turn the larger of the two, and do likewise with the .ij. veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	In regard to the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	In relation to the health of the tongue
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the healer is that the disease seizes between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts up the tongue, and looks at each side with a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So heal both, and do not become too perfect, for soon the veins will be black.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins that are commonly used are done according to .ij. ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where it pierces with all kinds of flames, or olive oil, so as to call it "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and thin according to the width and the stretching of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is called "mirtin", and it is wide as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is a skill to open the veins of thick blood which appear on the flat surface of the head and contain thick blood and trouble;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the flame of olive oil:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle to point out, and it is for saving the subtle veins, or there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The salve of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so helps with diseases that are in the throat, and where the collar, and where the chest, and where the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon that he cauterize, and that he bandage it with wool, and that he not pierce the artery which is exposed.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he stops the artery, and the flow of blood comes, if it is necessary to cauterize, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it must not be struck by the flame, but cut as Anesile.

ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	If you want to prevent it from happening again, or if you are injured at the base of the arm, it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and hold the wound in fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you can recognize the injury's location, so that you extract the arm, and touch the spot until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the spot with a pen, then extract the arm, and hold the wound in fire as we have said.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not wound in the artery when you see it moved from its place, for that is the artery: therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	and if you see spitting up high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery:

se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	lay your arm down, and leave it, and do not move the sick person; and be afraid, and do not move it until he is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if there is no blood coming out, and he goes away, and the medicine does not reach him, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of the shoulder retains it; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fir tree and split it, and take one half and tie it well together until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding has stopped, that is good; if not, apply the powder that stops blood, as we have said;

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The doctor will instruct the patient to let the veins empty of blood between the shoulder blade and the neck, and between the heart and the collarbone.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	For it is composed of the bazillical and cephalic parts, as we have said;

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the treatment depends on your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about a doctor is that medicine should only be used for the sake of maintaining health.

Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The saint who is free from diseases has no specific time for fasting or eating, but it should be done at all times and in all seasons.

que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein stops bleeding.

Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this pain is that the patient goes in or out of the water, and pulls it off the ankle. iiij. two must twist,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so that you can feel it with all your fingers, and running across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and worth more than you can pay, for the leg is out, and it is very heavy to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, neither does any rain of him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the small bow, and keep away from the water;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make the blood flow so that you see it, and then draw the arrow, and put cotton on it and hold it in; now it is cured.
Des sainies de ventouse	Suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or of ark-glass, or of pottery; and the suction is made in one of two ways: either by injuring and pulling out blood, or without injuring.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation, which is not to hurt according to .ij. ways: or it is on all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation which is made by hurting and by extraction of blood so is made in 13 parts from the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	from where one is all at the top; and the others are around the throat;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and 2 in 2 places on the throat; and the windpipe under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the vacuum of the shoulder joint; and the vacuum on the shoulders;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the vacuums of the arms; and the vacuums of the legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the vacuums of the ankles; and the vacuum treatment does not treat blood flow, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the carriage,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and so you don't weaken yourself at all, as is done with vein bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be amined, or any fire or heat in any disease that comes from excess, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it is necessary to ventilate, or because of habits, if we administer it every hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and burn it and put it in each ten;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to ventilate, become very heavy;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who have repletion and pain in their face, and in their head, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who drink a drop of blood in their mouth, and have flown away with the tongue, and are satisfied with blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are any such people who think, and see by no blood or vomit or death or similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to be breathed after .iij. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saint of music helps the greyness of the head ... if it comes to the eyes, and does not come until the whole body has been evacuated.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in the place of the head of the skull,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not suit anyone who has a cold complexions to use it, or who has had a fever, because this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for that reason neither the old nor those who have had cold illnesses should use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured of it often become confused, and for that reason the ventilating should be placed a little further back due to the confusion caused by the cure.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The venting of the wind comes from the neck, which is in place under the chin and the bazoo, and for this reason it causes irritation to the pit.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and a cutting of the channel of the stomach, and all, and filling up;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and so it is necessary to push back, for if it holds too firmly, then either hunger or the stomach or both.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The venting of the wind comes from the neck, which is in pain under the chin, and causes blindness and dizziness, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the place of the shrine of the basilica; and you must command the physician that he express his hand to apply, that he not cut the artery, and do not cause the blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilations of the mouth cause disease of the mouth and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the shrines of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the shoulders cause disease that comes from heat and filling up.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilations of the collar cause as much as the three veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for she brings blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for the blood vessels and nerves are easily damaged, and the veins and arteries are exposed.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back should not be placed too deeply, and should not hurt the foundations or the nerves, and it must be large and of iron, for its job is to suck well; and perhaps, if it were too delicate, it would break; and would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs should open widely, for they bring blood from all over the body, and cause pain to the old nerves, and the uterus, and the bladder, and draw forth flowers; and are in front of the 12th rib and the 12th shin bone, and after a long use, they weaken the body and bring about many diseases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Here is the translation of the text from Old French to English:
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is thick, so it is necessary to hurt .ij. times: the first time to soften the path of the great pain.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick, so it is necessary to hurt the third time; and when we want to squeeze the little pain a little at a time, we must suffer a great deal once only.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to squeeze the pain, so we should start again; and if it is thick, so we must firmly hold it, and the end should be that the scream be heard all at once.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover those who have thick and tough skin, and who are prone to scrofula, with the oil of vitriol that softens and dissolves.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is seared, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or gourd seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is burned, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, then use almond oil, or balsamite oil, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if there is someone who has an injured shoulder and chest, and it must be tended with oil and wide fabric, then do not put oil on.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the windification with pink water, or cold water, or water of blackberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other kind.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture, if it raises thus, or with water of mistletoe, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if there are great excesses, they rise with old wine, or water of sedge, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or other things like them.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and do not get wet before the bath or bathe, but after the bath an hour or .ij.; and do not sleep after the wind-up,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is good that he warm himself, when he must be winded, and when he has been winded.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are coleric, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he prunes cold things, like grapes and endives and lettuce by the sea, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and a little pork, and cheese, and wet meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, if they drink honey syrup, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and little pork, and little piglets and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and let him urinate when he feels the urge, if he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is good to give some people a strong or musk-scented unguent before or after urination, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be careful of the sun, but it is useful only for those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are used to hurt are those that are placed on the liver, and the mouse, and the podagra, and the belly, and the bouds, and the reins, and the hinch, for that member does not suffer to be hurt on the outs.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does not do it but to attract blood from one member to another.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the teats when the milk comes; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put leeches on the belly and on the bouds to weaken the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and the bone the pain, when it has surgery or stone, if by its own virtue the surgery is attracted or deserts the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus do so because when you put it on the liver and on the mouse when there is repressed wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are emptied only to suck; and never are they emptied together fire, and never are they filled with fresh water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as such diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way the suction cup is filled with hot water, or water in which he has cooked herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be 1 1/4 inches wide and half a palm long, and it should have a small hole at the center, about as big as an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be of iron, smooth before so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a crossbar of iron or of steel, to hold a candle in place;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and are great and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the leeches of children are other than those of old people, and thin ones than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And it is necessary to put this leech on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the wax candle or .i. linen thread, and place it between the leech and the limb where the leech is to be placed,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the bellows so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and your two hands are on the hole that we have said, so that when you blow, if there is steam, and then take off the bellows;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the poultice as before, and start it over again, if you need to;
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bellows which is amined for pleurisy, with all water, has no verge or hole, and is amined only when it is plain of water, and is put on the limb as little as possible;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	And these are not suited for use except in limbs where it is difficult to place suction cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on naked legs, such as two or three toes, and other similar parts.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of their use is that when you find suction cups that are in clear, non-runny water, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a broth of sweet water until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then poultice it with vinegar and poultice, then rub the limb until it is red, and put poultices on it;
